\doxysubsection{Description détaillée}
The scss compiler and parser.

Converting SCSS to CSS is a three stage process. The incoming file is parsed by {\ttfamily Parser} into a syntax tree, then it is compiled into another tree representing the CSS structure by {\ttfamily Compiler}. The CSS tree is fed into a formatter, like {\ttfamily Formatter} which then outputs CSS as a string.

During the first compile, all values are {\itshape reduced}, which means that their types are brought to the lowest form before being dump as strings. This handles math equations, variable dereferences, and the like.

The {\ttfamily compile} function of {\ttfamily Compiler} is the entry point.

In summary\+:

The {\ttfamily Compiler} class creates an instance of the parser, feeds it SCSS code, then transforms the resulting tree to a CSS tree. This class also holds the evaluation context, such as all available mixins and variables at any given time.

The {\ttfamily Parser} class is only concerned with parsing its input.

The {\ttfamily Formatter} takes a CSS tree, and dumps it to a formatted string, handling things like indentation. SCSS compiler

\begin{DoxyAuthor}{Auteur}
Leaf Corcoran \href{mailto:leafot@gmail.com}{\texttt{ leafot@gmail.\+com}}
\end{DoxyAuthor}
@final Extending the Compiler is deprecated

\Hypertarget{class_scss_php_1_1_scss_php_1_1_compiler_a73dc40a9aa264a46a26f02222ca640d0}\label{class_scss_php_1_1_scss_php_1_1_compiler_a73dc40a9aa264a46a26f02222ca640d0} 
\index{Compiler@{Compiler}!compileBlock@{compileBlock}}
\index{compileBlock@{compileBlock}!Compiler@{Compiler}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{compileBlock()}{compileBlock()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily compile\+Block (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_scss_php_1_1_scss_php_1_1_block}{Block}}}]{\$block }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}}

Recursively compiles a block.

A block is analogous to a CSS block in most cases. A single SCSS document is encapsulated in a block when parsed, but it does not have parent tags so all of its children appear on the root level when compiled.

Blocks are made up of selectors and children.

The children of a block are just all the blocks that are defined within.

Compiling the block involves pushing a fresh environment on the stack, and iterating through the props, compiling each one.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{Voir également}
Compiler\+::compile\+Child()
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\index{Compiler@{Compiler}!compileValue@{compileValue}}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{compileValue()}{compileValue()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily compile\+Value (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{\$value,  }\item[{}]{\$quote = {\ttfamily true} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Compiles a primitive value into a CSS property value.

Values in scssphp are typed by being wrapped in arrays, their format is typically\+: \begin{DoxyVerb}array(type, contents [, additional_contents]*)
\end{DoxyVerb}
 The input is expected to be reduced. This function will not work on things like expressions and variables.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily extract\+Relationship\+From\+Fragment (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{array}]{\$fragment }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}}

Extract a relationship from the fragment.

When extracting the last portion of a selector we will be left with a fragment which may end with a direction relationship combinator. This method will extract the relationship fragment and return it along side the rest.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Paramètres}
array & {\em \$fragment} & The selector fragment maybe ending with a direction relationship combinator.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Renvoie}
array The selector without the relationship fragment if any, the relationship fragment. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

Gets the keywords of an argument list.

Keys in the returned array are normalized names (underscores are replaced with dashes) without the leading {\ttfamily \$}. Calling this helper with anything that an argument list received for a rest argument of the function argument declaration is not supported.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily static is\+Css\+Import (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{\$url }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}

Detects whether the import is a CSS import.

For legacy reasons, custom importers are called for those, allowing them to replace them with an actual Sass import. However this behavior is deprecated. Custom importers are expected to return null when they receive a CSS import.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Paramètres}
string & {\em \$url} & \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\index{Compiler@{Compiler}!setCharset@{setCharset}}
\index{setCharset@{setCharset}!Compiler@{Compiler}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{setCharset()}{setCharset()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily set\+Charset (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{\$charset }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Configures the handling of non-\/\+ASCII outputs.

If \$charset is {\ttfamily true}, this will include a {\ttfamily @charset} declaration or a UTF-\/8 \href{https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byte_order_mark\#UTF-8}{\texttt{ byte-\/order mark}} if the stylesheet contains any non-\/\+ASCII characters. Otherwise, it will never include a {\ttfamily @charset} declaration or a byte-\/order mark.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Paramètres}
bool & {\em \$charset} & \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Renvoie}
void 
\end{DoxyReturn}
